<div id="S001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec-type_intro NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i3" class="section-heading-2">1. Introduction</h2>
 <p>The detection of explosives in places where they are likely to be present in the shortest possible time will prevent many innocent victims. Minimizing the time and the effort to detect one of the explosive needs to increase the number of searchers and the coordination process among them. The case of the randomly located object with a known distribution on the real line has been discussed by Reyniers&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0001" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>1</a></span>,<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0002" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>2</a></span>]. She considered two unit speeds searchers aim to find this object in the shortest possible time. In addition, Mohamed et al.&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0003" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>3</a></span>,<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0004" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>4</a></span>] studied this problem for the hidden object which has a known distribution in an open area.</p>
 <p>On the other hand, for a stochastically moving object, El-Hadidy and Abou-Gabal&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0005" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>5</a></span>] and El-Hadidy and Alzulaibani&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0006" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>6</a></span>,<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0007" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>7</a></span>] used a linear coordinated search technique to present a finite search plan which minimizes the first collision time expected value between one of the searchers and the stochastically moving object. Moreover, this technique is applied by using the Bayesian approach (see, e.g.&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0008 CIT0009 CIT0010 CIT0011" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>8–11</a></span>]). Earlier, many interesting methods to track the stochastically moving object have been presented by Dai et al.&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0012" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>12</a></span>] and Deilami et al.&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0013" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>13</a></span>]. Besides that, Mohamed et al.&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0014" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>14</a></span>,<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0015" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>15</a></span>], Mohamed and El-Hadidy&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0016" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>16</a></span>], Mohamed and El-Hadidy&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0017" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>17</a></span>], Beltagy and El-Hadidy&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0018" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>18</a></span>], Abou-Gabal and El-Hadidy&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0019" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>19</a></span>], Mohamed et al.&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0020" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>20</a></span>], Kassem and El-Hadidy&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0021" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>21</a></span>], El-Hadidy and El-Bagoury&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0022" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>22</a></span>], El-Hadidy&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0023 CIT0024 CIT0025 CIT0026 CIT0027 CIT0028 CIT0029 CIT0030 CIT0031" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>23–31</a></span>], El-Hadidy and Alzulaibani&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0006" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>6</a></span>,<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0007" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>7</a></span>], and El-Hadidy et al.&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0032" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>32</a></span>] provided many different mathematical treatments of this issue in both cases stochastically moving and hidden objects.</p>
 <p>This paper aims to coordinate the search technique that allows the <i>M</i>-searchers <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">

 <div class="hidden rs_skip" id="figureFootNote-F0001">
  <div class="figureFootNote-F0001"></div>
 </div>
 <p></p>
 <p>In this work, Section&nbsp;<a href="#S002">2</a> explains the problem and presents the expected reward cost of detection. In Section&nbsp;<a href="#S003">3</a>, the optimal search policy that minimizes the expected reward cost of detection is presented after considering the Circular Normal distribution of the object's position. A discussion of the results and future works is presented in the conclusion part.</p>
</div>
<div id="S002" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i5" class="section-heading-2">2. Problem formulation</h2>
 <p>The mathematical model of this problem is formulated by considering the discounted search effort reward. This model gives the expected value of the discounted effort reward for detection in one of <i>N</i>-disjoint and not identical regions <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
   <noscript>
    <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0006.gif" alt="">
   </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0006.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
   <math>
    <msub>
     <mi>
      R
     </mi>
     <mrow>
      <mi>
       ℓ
      </mi>
     </mrow>
    </msub><mo>
     ,
    </mo><mi>
     ℓ
    </mi><mo>
     =
    </mo><mn>
     1
    </mn><mo>
     ,
    </mo><mn>
     2
    </mn><mo>
     ,
    </mo><mo>
     …
    </mo><mo>
     ,
    </mo><mi>
     N
    </mi><mo>
     .
    </mo>
   </math></span></p>
 <div id="S002-S2001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i6">2.1. The searching process</h3>
  <p><i>The search space:</i> The space is divided into <i>N</i>-disjoint and not identical regions <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0007.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0007.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <msub>
      <mi>
       R
      </mi>
      <mrow>
       <mi>
        ℓ
       </mi>
      </mrow>
     </msub><mo>
      ,
     </mo><mi>
      ℓ
     </mi><mo>
      =
     </mo><mn>
      1
     </mn><mo>
      ,
     </mo><mn>
      2
     </mn><mo>
      ,
     </mo><mo>
      …
     </mo><mo>
      ,
     </mo><mi>
      N
     </mi>
    </math></span>. Each region has two roads intersected at the centre of this region. These roads divide the region into four identical parts. The two roads are considered as <i>x</i> and <i>y</i> axes (see Figure&nbsp;<a href="#F0001">1</a>). Here, the report for the object position is given at <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0008.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0008.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mo>
      (
     </mo><mn>
      0
     </mn><mo>
      ,
     </mo><mn>
      0
     </mn><mo>
      )
     </mo>
    </math></span>.</p>
  <p><i>The object:</i> The object is randomly located in one of these regions with symmetric distribution about <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0009.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0009.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mo>
      (
     </mo><mn>
      0
     </mn><mo>
      ,
     </mo><mn>
      0
     </mn><mo>
      )
     </mo>
    </math></span>.</p>
  <p><i>The means of search:</i> Let <i>M</i> searchers start the searching process for the object from the <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0010.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0010.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mo>
      (
     </mo><mn>
      0
     </mn><mo>
      ,
     </mo><mn>
      0
     </mn><mo>
      )
     </mo>
    </math></span> in each region. Each region has an even number of searchers. The searchers go along the two axes (<span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0011.gif" alt="">
    </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0011.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
    <math>
     <mo>
      +
     </mo><mi>
      v
     </mi><mi>
      e
     </mi>
    </math></span> and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
    <noscript>
     <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0012.gif" alt="">

    Corollary 2.2 
    <p>In the case of two searchers, one of them searches the sectors in the right part of the <i>y</i>-axis and the other searches the sectors in the left part. In addition, the object has symmetric distribution and <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
      <noscript>
       <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0133.gif" alt="">
      </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0133.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
      <math>
       <msubsup>
        <mi>
         d
        </mi>
        <mrow>
         <mi>
          ℓ
         </mi>
        </mrow>
        <mrow>
         <mi>
          i
         </mi>
        </mrow>
       </msubsup><mo>
        =
       </mo><mfrac>
        <mn>
         1
        </mn>
        <mn>
         2
        </mn>
       </mfrac>
      </math></span>. Then, the expected value of the time for the searchers to return to the origin&nbsp;after the object detection is <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve">
      <noscript>
       <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_m0002.gif" alt="">
      </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_m0002.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"><span class="disp_formula_label_div"><span id="M0002" class="disp-formula-label">(2) </span></span></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula disp-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">

   <p>The above result shows that this technique is more suitable to detect an important object (like a bomb or a person in a wilderness area) by using <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
     <noscript>
      <img src="/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0148.gif" alt="">
     </noscript><img src="//:0" alt="" class="mml-formula" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;image&quot;, &quot;src&quot; : &quot;/na101/home/literatum/publisher/tandf/journals/content/tusc20/2020/tusc20.v014.i01/16583655.2020.1747217/20210529/images/tusc_a_1747217_ilm0148.gif&quot;}"><span class="mml-formula"></span></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula inline-formula rs_preserve"><img src="//:0" alt="" data-formula-source="{&quot;type&quot; : &quot;mathjax&quot;}">
     <math>
      <msub>
       <mi>
        q
       </mi>
       <mrow>
        <mi>
         ℓ
        </mi>
       </mrow>
      </msub>
     </math></span> searchers.</p>
  </div>
 </div>

     &nbsp;
    </mtext><mi>
     i
    </mi><mo>
     ,
    </mo><mi>

    </mo><mn>
     1
    </mn><mo>

 <div id="S003-S2001" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2">
  <h3 class="section-heading-3" id="_i33">3.1. The case of the initial position given by a Circular Normal distribution</h3>
  <p>In all search strategies, we consider that the debris diffusion of an aeroplane crash over the oceans and seas have a Circular Normal distribution, why? By considering the disaster of Air France Flight 447, Stone et al.&nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0034" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>34</a></span>] answered this question. They proved that all impact points of debris are found within a 20 nautical mile radius circle from the crashed point. After they analysed the data about these impact points of debris, they found that the distribution of these points is a Circular Normal distribution with centre at the last known position. Thus, we let <i>X</i>, <i>Y</i> are two independent random variables that represent the last position of the object (black box), and they have a Circular Normal distribution with joint probability density function which considered in &nbsp;[<span class="ref-lnk lazy-ref"><a data-rid="CIT0027" data-reflink="_i39 _i40" href="#"><span class="off-screen">Citation</span>27</a></span>]: <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image disp-formula rs_preserve">

<div id="S004" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1">
 <h2 id="_i38" class="section-heading-2">4. Conclusion and future work</h2>
 <p>We discussed the coordinated search technique to find a hidden object in the plane. The position of the object is given by two independent random variables <i>X</i>, <i>Y</i>. The expected value of the reward cost is given in Theorem&nbsp;2.1. Theorem&nbsp;2.3 presented the total expected reward cost of detection for any even number of searchers in one of the non-identical <i>N</i>-regions. By assuming the Circular Normal distribution of the object position, we obtain the optimal values of <span class="NLM_disp-formula-image inline-formula rs_preserve">
